KNEE 1. ACL Reconstruction (Hamstring Graft) Phase 1 — Immediate Post-op (Week 0–2)
🎯 GOALS
• Control pain & swelling
• Achieve full passive knee extension
• Quadriceps activation
• Independent ambulation with crutches
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No active knee extension 0–90°
• Avoid hamstring loading (graft protection)
• PWB with crutches
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Quadriceps Sets (Isometric) 3 × 20 reps, 5-sec hold
Flatten back of knee to bed, feel VMO contract
Ankle Pumps 3 × 30 reps Reduce DVT risk, improve circulation
Straight Leg Raise (SLR) 3 × 15 reps Lock knee before lifting, no lag allowed
Heel Slides (AAROM Flexion) 3 × 15 reps Slide heel toward buttocks, hold 2 sec at end range
Passive Knee Extension (prone hang)
3 × 5 min Let gravity achieve full extension
Patellar Mobilisation 2 × 2 min Medial, lateral, superior glides — pain-
free
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full passive extension achieved
• SLR without extension lag
• Swelling <1+ on effusion scale
Phase 2 — Early Strengthening (Week 2–6)
🎯 GOALS
• 0–120° ROM
• Normalise gait without crutches
• Begin CKC loading
• Neuromuscular re-education
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid OKC knee extension 0–60°
• No pivoting or cutting
• Monitor effusion with activity
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 6
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Mini Squats (0–45°) 3 × 15 reps Knees track over 2nd toe, weight through heels
Step-Ups (10 cm box) 3 × 15 reps each leg Lead with affected leg, control descent
Leg Press (60–90°) 3 × 15 reps, light load Bilateral then unilateral, avoid locking out
Terminal Knee Extension (band) 3 × 20 reps Focus on last 20° — VMO activation
Hip Abduction — Side-lying 3 × 20 reps Maintain pelvic stability, control return
Calf Raises (bilateral) 3 × 20 reps Full ROM, slow eccentric phase
Stationary Bike (low resistance) 20 min ROM & cardiovascular — no pain
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full ROM 0–120°
• Single-leg stance ≥30 sec
• Normal gait pattern without device
Phase 3 — Advanced Strengthening (Week 6–12)
🎯 GOALS
• Limb Symmetry Index (LSI) >70%
• Begin jogging
• Develop strength & power
• Proprioception training
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No change-of-direction sport
• Monitor for effusion post-exercise
• Gradual plyometric loading
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Bulgarian Split Squat 4 × 10 reps each Front foot flat, torso upright, 90° knee flexion
Romanian Deadlift 4 × 10 reps Hip hinge pattern, neutral spine, feel hamstring load
Lateral Band Walks 3 × 15 steps each direction
Maintain squat position, band around ankles
Single-Leg Press 4 × 12 reps Progressive loading, track limb symmetry
Box Step-Down 3 × 12 reps each Slow 5-sec eccentric, control valgus collapse
Double-leg Squat Jump 3 × 10 reps Soft landing, absorb force through hips and knees
Forward Hop (non-reactive) 3 × 8 reps Stick landing 3 sec before next hop
Linear Jog Program Start 10 min, progress weekly
Even surface, no cutting — pain-free
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• LSI ≥80% quad & hamstring strength
• Hop test symmetry ≥80%
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 7
• Jog pain-free 30 min
Phase 4 — Return to Sport (Month 4–9)
🎯 GOALS
• LSI ≥90% all hop tests
• Sport-specific agility
• Psychological readiness
• Full return to unrestricted sport
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Clear psychological readiness (ACL-RSI score)
• Minimum 9 months post-op for contact sport
• Gradual reintroduction to team training
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
T-Agility Test Drills 4–6 sets Progressive speed increase over weeks
Reactive Change-of-Direction 3 × 10 reps Controlled, then progress to reactive cues
Plyometric Progression (single-
leg)
3 × 8 reps Lateral hops, bounding, depth jumps — master each before progressing
Sport-Specific Drills 3 × 5 min blocks Cutting, deceleration, sport movement patterns
Strength Maintenance (Gym) 3 × week Maintain gains achieved in Phase 3
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• LSI ≥90% quad/hamstring/hop
• ACL-RSI ≥65
• Clearance from surgeon + physio
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Grindem H et al. (2016). Simple decision rules can reduce reinjury risk by 84%. BJSM.
• Kyritsis P et al. (2016). Likelihood of ACL graft rupture: not meeting six clinical discharge criteria. BJSM.
• Logerstedt D et al. (2017). Knee Stability and Movement Coordination Impairments: Knee Ligament Sprain Revision 2017. JOSPT.
• van Melick N et al. (2016). Evidence-based clinical practice update: Practice guidelines for anterior cruciate ligament rehabilitation. BJSM.

2. ACL Tear — Conservative Management Phase 1 — Acute (Week 0–2)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce effusion & pain
• Achieve full extension
• Restore basic quad activation
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid pivoting/cutting
• Brace if instability present
• No impact loading
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Quad Sets 3 × 20 reps Isometric quad contraction, focus on VMO
SLR (Flexion) 3 × 15 reps Maintain full knee extension throughout
Ankle Pumps 3 × 30 reps Circulation and swelling control
Prone Knee Hang (extension) 3 × 5 min Achieve neutral 0° extension
Cryotherapy 15–20 min every 2h Post-exercise swelling management
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full extension
• Minimal effusion
• SLR without lag
Phase 2 — Strengthening (Week 2–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM
• Symmetrical strength
• Normalise gait
• Functional stability
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid high-risk pivot sports without brace
• Monitor giving-way episodes
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Wall Squat (45–60°) 3 × 20 reps Isometric hold 5 sec at bottom
Step-ups 3 × 15 reps each Step height progresses 10→15→20 cm
Hip Strengthening Circuit 3 × 15 reps each exercise
Abductors, extensors, external rotators
TKE (band) 3 × 20 reps Terminal knee extension focus on VMO
Single-leg Balance 3 × 30 sec Eyes open then closed, unstable surface progression
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 9
Stationary Bike 20–30 min No pain, moderate resistance
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Limb symmetry >80%
• No giving way with daily activities
• Single leg squat with good control
Phase 3 — Functional & Return to Sport (Week 8–16+)
🎯 GOALS
• Return to sport decision
• Full strength symmetry
• Agility & confidence
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• If giving way persists → surgical review
• Use brace for high-risk sport return if needed
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Squat 4 × 12 reps Control valgus, depth to 60° minimum
Plyometrics (bilateral then unilateral)
3 × 10 reps Progressive — jump, land, bound, hop
Agility Ladder 3 × 4 patterns Speed progression, sharp direction changes
Running Program Progressive Straight → curves → sprints → change of direction
Sport-Specific Training Full session Reintegrate sport skills with team
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Hop test LSI ≥90%
• No episodes of instability
• Sport clearance
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Grindem H et al. (2014). Nonsurgical or surgical treatment of ACL injuries: knee function, sports participation, and knee reinjury. JOSPT.
• Frobell RB et al. (2013). Treatment for acute anterior cruciate ligament tear: five year outcome of randomised trial. BMJ.
• Moksnes H & Risberg MA. (2009). Performance-based functional evaluation of non-operative and operative treatment after anterior cruciate ligament injury. Scand J Med Sci Sports.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 10
3. Meniscus Repair (Post-operative) Phase 1 — Protection (Week 0–6)
🎯 GOALS
• Protect repair
• Control effusion
• Maintain quad activation
• Toe-touch weight bearing
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• NWB or TTWB only
• No flexion beyond 90°
• No squatting or pivoting
• Crutches mandatory
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Quad Sets 4 × 20 reps Critical for preventing quad atrophy during NWB
SLR (4 planes) 3 × 15 reps each Flexion, abduction, adduction, extension
Ankle Pumps 3 × 30 reps DVT prevention
AAROM Flexion (to 90° only) 3 × 15 reps Heel slides, stop at 90° — respect repair
Stationary Bike (seat HIGH) 15 min Minimal knee flexion, low resistance — after week 4
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• No effusion increase with activity
• Full extension maintained
• Week 6 surgeon clearance
Phase 2 — Progressive Loading (Week 6–12)
🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM 0–130°
• WBAT progressing to FWB
• Functional strength
• Normalise gait
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid deep squat >90° until week 10
• No running yet
• Monitor for joint line pain
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Mini Squats (0–60°) 3 × 15 reps Progress range weekly, bilateral first
Leg Press (bilateral) 3 × 15 reps 60–90° range, controlled
Step-ups (forward & lateral) 3 × 15 each 10 cm → 15 cm box progression
Single-leg Balance 3 × 45 sec Stable then unstable surface
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 11
Hip Strengthening 3 × 15 each Abductors and extensors — key for knee stability
Pool Walking 20 min Offload joint while gaining ROM and strength
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full ROM achieved
• FWB without pain
• Normal gait without assistive device
Phase 3 — Return to Function (Month 3–6)
🎯 GOALS
• Return to running (month 4)
• Sport-specific training
• Full symmetrical function
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No contact sport before month 6
• Avoid deep pivoting positions until month 5
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Squat 4 × 12 reps Full depth, control valgus
Running Program Walk-jog progression Begin month 4 — even surface, build duration
Plyometrics 3 × 10 reps Bilateral jumps first, then unilateral hops
Agility Drills 3 sets Carioca, T-drill, shuttle runs
Sport-Specific Skills Progressive Full sport return month 6 with surgeon clearance
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• LSI >90% strength & hop tests
• No pain with sport activity
• Surgeon clearance at 6 months
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Shea KG et al. (2004). Meniscus repair: outcomes and goals. AAOS.
• Mordecai SC et al. (2014). Treatment of meniscal tears: An evidence based approach. World J Orthop.
• Salata MJ et al. (2010). A systematic review of clinical outcomes in patients undergoing meniscectomy. Am J Sports Med.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 12
4. Patellofemoral Pain Syndrome (PFPS) Phase 1 — Pain Reduction (Week 0–3)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce anterior knee pain
• Restore pain-free ROM
• Patient education on load management
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid pain >4/10 with exercise
• No deep squatting or stairs initially
• Patellar taping as adjunct
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Straight Leg Raise 3 × 15 reps VMO activation without PFJ stress
Hip Abduction (side-lying) 3 × 20 reps Key — hip weakness major driver of PFPS
Hip External Rotation (clamshell) 3 × 20 reps Band around knees, control movement
Quad Sets + Biofeedback 3 × 20 reps VMO focus, biofeedback if available
Stationary Bike (pain-free range) 15–20 min High seat to limit flexion load
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain ≤2/10 with ADLs
• Full pain-free ROM
• Ready for CKC loading
Phase 2 — Strengthening (Week 3–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Hip and quad strengthening
• Neuromuscular control
• Load tolerance for stairs & squatting
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor for pain increase post-exercise
• Avoid OKC exercises if painful
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Wall Squat (0–60°) 3 × 20 reps Focus on hip-knee-foot alignment
Step-down (eccentric focus) 3 × 15 reps Slow 4-sec descent, control knee valgus
Hip Thrust 3 × 15 reps Glute activation and posterior chain loading
Lateral Band Walk 3 × 15 steps each Hip external rotator and abductor activation
TKE (band) 3 × 20 reps VMO activation in functional position
Running on flat surface Start 10 min Pain-free only — cadence focus
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 13
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Stairs pain-free
• Single-leg squat controlled
• Running 20 min pain-free
Phase 3 — Return to Sport (Week 8–16)
🎯 GOALS
• Sport-specific loading
• Full return to running and sport
• Long-term self-management
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Maintain hip strengthening long-term
• Manage training load spikes
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Squat Progression 4 × 12 reps Add load, depth, and speed progressively
Plyometrics (bilateral → unilateral)
3 × 10 reps Ensure pain-free landing mechanics
Running Program Progressive duration & intensity
10% rule for weekly mileage increase
Sport-Specific Drills Full sessions Cutting, jumping, sport movement patterns
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain-free with all sport demands
• Confident return to training
• Self-managed home program
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Crossley KM et al. (2016). 2016 Patellofemoral pain consensus statement from the 4th International Patellofemoral Pain Research Retreat. BJSM.
• Rathleff MS et al. (2015). Hip muscle strengthening for patellofemoral pain. Am J Sports Med.
• Powers CM. (2010). The influence of abnormal hip mechanics on knee injury: a biomechanical perspective. JOSPT.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 14
5. Patellar Tendinopathy Phase 1 — Load Reduction & Isometrics (Week 0–4)
🎯 GOALS
• Pain reduction
• Tendon loading via isometrics
• Reduce reactive tendinopathy
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid stretching tendon
• Avoid high load eccentric initially if reactive
• Manage training load
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Isometric Leg Press (70° knee flexion)
5 × 45 sec hold, 80% effort
Immediate analgesic effect — key exercise
Isometric Wall Squat 5 × 45 sec hold Same benefit as leg press if no machine available
Hip Strengthening 3 × 15 reps Glutes, hip abductors — reduce tendon load
Upper body & non-painful conditioning
As tolerated Maintain fitness without tendon provocation
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• VISA-P score improvement
• Pain ≤3/10 with isometrics
• Morning stiffness reducing
Phase 2 — Heavy Slow Resistance (Week 4–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Tendon structural adaptation
• Strength gains
• Return to light sport-specific loading
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid plyometrics
• Monitor 24h pain response after loading
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Leg Press (heavy, slow) 4 × 6 reps, 3-sec up, 4-sec down
Heavy slow resistance — gold standard
Hack Squat 4 × 6 reps, slow tempo Progressive load increase weekly
Spanish Squat (isometric) 4 × 45 sec Band around fixed point, hip hinge position
Step-ups (heavy) 3 × 10 reps each High box, controlled eccentric
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 15
• VISA-P ≥60
• Tolerating heavy loading without spike
• Ready for plyometric introduction
Phase 3 — Energy Storage & Return to Sport (Week 8–16)
🎯 GOALS
• Plyometric tolerance
• Sport-specific jumping and landing
• Full return to sport
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Gradual plyometric loading — volume before intensity
• Monitor VISA-P monthly
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Drop Squat 3 × 10 reps Fast loading — energy storage introduction
Double-leg Hop 3 × 10 reps Stick landing, then continuous hops
Single-leg Hop Progression 3 × 8 reps Forward, lateral, diagonal — pain <3/10
Sport-Specific Jumping / Landing Full drills Jump-specific to sport (volleyball net, basketball layup, etc.)
Return to Jumping Sport Progressive sessions 10% volume increase per week
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• VISA-P ≥80
• Pain-free with max sport demands
• Symmetrical hop tests
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Cook JL & Purdam CR. (2009). Is tendon pathology a continuum? BJSM.
• Visnes H & Bahr R. (2007). The evolution of eccentric training as treatment for patellar tendinopathy. BJSM.
• Rio E et al. (2015). Isometric exercise induces analgesia and reduces inhibition in patellar tendinopathy. BJSM.
• Beyer R et al. (2015). Heavy slow resistance versus eccentric training as treatment for Achilles tendinopathy. Am J Sports Med.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 16
6. MCL Sprain (Grade II) Phase 1 — Protection (Week 0–2)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce pain and swelling
• Protect healing ligament
• Maintain quad activation
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Valgus stress brace recommended
• Avoid valgus loading
• Partial weight bearing
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Quad Sets 3 × 20 reps Prevent quad atrophy
SLR (4 planes) 3 × 15 reps Maintain hip and quad strength
Stationary Bike (pain-free) 15 min High seat, low resistance, reduce swelling
Cryotherapy 15 min × 3–4/day Swelling management
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain ≤3/10 at rest
• Able to FWB with brace
Phase 2 — Strengthening (Week 2–6)
🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM
• Valgus control
• FWB without brace
• CKC strengthening
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid valgus collapse in all exercises
• Progress load gradually
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Mini Squats 3 × 15 reps Knees straight, no valgus collapse
Step-ups (forward & lateral) 3 × 15 reps Control medial knee position
Hip Abductor Strengthening 3 × 20 reps Critical to reduce valgus stress on MCL
TKE (band) 3 × 20 reps Quad activation, controlled alignment
Single-leg Balance 3 × 30 sec Progress to unstable surface
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• FWB pain-free
• No valgus instability with ADL
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 17
Phase 3 — Return to Sport (Week 6–12)
🎯 GOALS
• Full sport return
• Cutting and pivoting tolerance
• Strength symmetry
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Consider functional brace for return to sport if Grade II+
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Squat 4 × 12 reps Full control, no valgus
Lateral Bounds 3 × 10 reps each Controlled landing, medial knee stability
Agility Drills 4 sets T-drill, shuttle, figure-8
Sport-Specific Training Full sessions Progressive return to full team training
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Hop test LSI >90%
• Confidence with valgus-loaded tasks
• Clearance from physio and MD
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Phisitkul P et al. (2006). MCL injuries of the knee: current concepts review. Iowa Orthop J.
• Indelicato PA. (1983). Non-operative treatment of complete tears of the MCL of the knee. JBJS.
• Wijdicks CA et al. (2010). Medial knee injury. Am J Sports Med.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 18
7. Total Knee Arthroplasty (TKA) Phase 1 — Acute Hospital (Day 0–3)
🎯 GOALS
• Pain management
• Achieve 0–90° ROM
• Independent mobility
• DVT prevention
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor for signs of DVT
• Weight bearing as tolerated (WBAT)
• Follow surgeon precautions
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Ankle Pumps 10 reps every hour DVT prevention — start immediately post-op
Quad Sets 3 × 20 reps Begin day 1 post-op
Heel Slides (AAROM) 3 × 15 reps Work toward 90° flexion
SLR 3 × 15 reps When quad sets pain-free
Sit-to-Stand 5 × per session Use armrests, controlled movement
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• 90° flexion
• Independent ambulation with frame
• Safe for discharge
Phase 2 — Home / Outpatient (Week 1–6)
🎯 GOALS
• 0–110° ROM
• FWB without aid
• Stair management
• Reduce swelling
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Ice post-exercise
• Avoid prolonged standing
• Take pain medication prior to PT
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Heel Slides 3 × 20 reps Work toward 110–120° daily
Terminal Knee Extension 3 × 20 reps Achieve full extension — critical goal
Mini Squats (0–60°) 3 × 15 reps Bilateral, progress depth weekly
Step-ups 3 × 15 reps each Low step initially (5 cm), increase gradually
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 19
Stationary Bike 20 min ROM and cardiovascular — begin week 3–4
Calf Raises 3 × 20 reps Bilateral, progress to single-leg
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• 0–110° ROM
• Walking independently on flat
• Negotiate stairs safely
Phase 3 — Strengthening (Month 2–3)
🎯 GOALS
• 0–120° ROM
• Functional strength
• Community ambulation
• Return to driving
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No high-impact sport (running, jumping) — check with surgeon
• Swimming and cycling recommended
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Leg Press 3 × 15 reps Progressive load, 60–90° range
Step-downs 3 × 15 reps Eccentric control, good hip-knee alignment
Single-leg Balance 3 × 45 sec Eyes open then closed
Cycling outdoors 20–30 min Low impact, excellent for ROM and strength
Pool Walking 30 min Offloads joint — excellent for early strengthening
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full ROM
• Community walking 30+ min
• Functional independence
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Artz N et al. (2015). Effectiveness of physiotherapy exercise following total knee replacement. BMC Musculoskelet Disord.
• Lenssen AF et al. (2008). Effectiveness of prolonged use of continuous passive motion after TKA. Phys Ther.
• Pua YH et al. (2015). Patient-reported outcomes and rehabilitation in TKA. JOSPT.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 20
8. PCL Tear — Conservative Phase 1 — Acute (Week 0–4)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce effusion
• Quad activation
• Protect posterior capsule
• FWB with brace
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• PCL brace with 0° extension stop
• No posterior tibial stress
• Avoid prone knee flexion
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Quad Sets 4 × 20 reps Quad dominance is protective for PCL — critical
SLR (flexion & extension) 3 × 15 reps No hamstring-loaded SLR
Leg Press (0–60° only) 3 × 15 reps Quad-dominant, avoid 90° — increases PCL stress
Stationary Bike (low resistance) 20 min High seat, low resistance, quad emphasis
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Effusion resolved
• Quad activation full
• Pain ≤2/10 with activity
Phase 2 — Progressive (Week 4–12)
🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM
• Quad strength 80% limb symmetry
• Functional gait
• Return to light activity
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid heavy hamstring loading
• No deep squatting in early phase
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Leg Press (progressive range) 4 × 12 reps Increase to 90° gradually after week 8
Step-ups 3 × 15 reps Quad-driven ascent and descent
Mini Squats 3 × 20 reps Progress depth and load
Hip strengthening 3 × 20 reps All planes — reduce knee joint load
Proprioception Training 3 × 30 sec Single-leg balance, perturbation training
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 21
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Symmetrical quad strength
• Normal gait
• No instability with daily tasks
Phase 3 — Return to Sport (Month 3–6)
🎯 GOALS
• Full sport return
• Functional hop tests ≥90%
• Hamstring-to-quad ratio within normal limits
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor for chronic posterior laxity
• May need functional brace for high-demand sport
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Running Program Progressive Begin month 3 — straight then curves
Plyometrics 3 × 10 reps Bilateral first, then unilateral progression
Sport-Specific Drills Full sessions Cutting, deceleration, change of direction
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• LSI ≥90%
• Pain-free sport participation
• Surgeon clearance
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Fanelli GC & Edson CJ. (1995). Posterior cruciate ligament injuries in trauma patients. Arthroscopy.
• Shelbourne KD & Davis TJ. (1999). Evaluation of knee stability before and after participation in a functional sports agility program during rehabilitation after ACL reconstruction. Am J Sports Med.

27. Iliotibial Band Syndrome Phase 1 — Reduce Irritation (Week 0–3)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce lateral knee pain
• Modify training load
• Address contributing factors
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid 30° knee flexion range (impingement zone)
• Reduce running mileage 50%
• Avoid downhill running
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Foam Roll IT Band / Glutes 2 × 2 min Release TFL and proximal IT band — not directly over knee
Hip Abductor Strengthening (standing)
3 × 20 reps Key driver — weak glute med increases ITB tension
Clamshell (band) 3 × 20 reps Hip ER strengthening
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain ≤3/10 with walking
• Reduce provocative running
Phase 2 — Hip Strengthening (Week 3–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Glute strength symmetry
• Running tolerance increasing
• Biomechanical correction
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor symptoms with each running session increase
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Squat 4 × 12 reps Control knee tracking — no valgus collapse
Lateral Band Walk 3 × 20 steps Functional hip abductor loading
Hip Thrust (heavy) 3 × 15 reps Glute max and med comprehensive loading
Running Gait Retraining 5–10% cadence increase
Reduces lateral knee stress — key intervention
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Running 30 min pain-free
• Single-leg squat controlled

• Full training volume
• Symptom-free sport participation
⚠ PRECAUTIONS

• Maintain hip strengthening permanently

10% weekly increase Build mileage gradually — monitor symptoms 24h post
Cross-training (bike, pool) Maintain cardiovascular fitness
Low ITB stress modalities

• Full training pain-free
• Race participation

• No plyometrics until this phase complete

Leg Press (heavy, slow) 4 × 6 reps, slow tempo 3-sec concentric, 4-sec eccentric
Hack Squat (slow tempo) 4 × 6 reps Heavy slow resistance protocol
Step-down (eccentric focus) 3 × 15 reps Slow eccentric — quad tendon loading
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• VISA-P ≥60
• Heavy loading tolerated without spike

🎯 GOALS
• Plyometric tolerance
• Sport-specific jumping/landing

• Full return

3 × 10 reps Progressive plyometric loading

3 × 10 reps, 5–10 sec hold
Sub-maximal — maintain activation without loading injured tissue

3 × 15 reps (light to moderate)
Concentric/eccentric loading — progress weekly
Neuromuscular Control Exercises 3 × 20–30 sec Balance and proprioception — single-leg or single-arm
Functional Movement Training 3 × 12 reps Squat, hinge, push, pull — based on injury region

• Full pain-free ROM
• Functional tasks independent

🎯 GOALS
• Full strength symmetry ≥90%
• Sport/work-specific demands met
• Prevention education
• Self-management strategies
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• 10% weekly load increase rule
• Maintain long-term exercise program
• Re-injury risk counselling
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Sport/Work-Specific Drills Progressive sessions Mirror demands of target activity
Plyometrics / Power Training 3 × 10 reps Bilateral → unilateral progression
Agility & Change of Direction 4 sets Speed progression — reactive cues added
Strength Maintenance Program 2–3 × per week Maintain gains to prevent recurrence
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Functional tests ≥90% symmetry
• Psychological readiness confirmed
• Return to full unrestricted activity

SHOULDER 9. Rotator Cuff Repair (Post-operative) Phase 1 — Passive Motion (Week 0–6)
🎯 GOALS
• Protect repair
• Prevent stiffness
• PROM: 140° flexion, 40° ER
• Pain management
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Sling at all times except exercise
• No AROM
• No lifting or pushing
• No internal rotation stress
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pendulum (Codman's) Exercises 3 × 2 min all planes Gravity-assisted distraction — no muscle activation
PROM Shoulder Flexion (supine) 3 × 15 reps to tolerance
Therapist-assisted, pain-free range
PROM ER (0° abduction) 3 × 15 reps Elbow at side, cane-assisted to 40°
Elbow ROM & grip strength 3 × 20 reps Maintain distal function while in sling
Scapular Retraction (isometric) 3 × 10 reps, 5 sec hold
Maintain scapular function
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• PROM: 140° flexion, 40° ER at neutral
• Pain controlled at rest
• Surgeon clearance at 6 weeks
Phase 2 — Active Assisted & Early Active (Week 6–12)
🎯 GOALS
• AAROM → AROM
• Rotator cuff activation
• Scapular stabilisation
• Progress to 150° flexion
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No lifting >1 kg
• No reaching behind back
• Avoid painful arcs
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 39
Pulleys (AAROM flexion) 3 × 20 reps Good arm assists — gradual range increase
Supine Active Flexion 3 × 15 reps Gravity-eliminated initially, progress to against gravity
ER with band (light resistance) 3 × 15 reps Elbow at side, slow controlled — infraspinatus/teres minor
Scapular Push-up (wall) 3 × 15 reps Serratus anterior — critical for scapular upward rotation
Side-lying ER 3 × 15 reps Light weight, focus on external rotators
Prone Y/T/W 3 × 12 reps Scapular stabilisers — no weight initially
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• AROM: 150° flexion
• ER to 60°
• No painful arc
Phase 3 — Strengthening (Month 3–6)
🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM
• Rotator cuff strength 80% symmetry
• Functional overhead activities
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No heavy overhead pressing
• Progress load slowly
• Monitor for impingement signs
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Shoulder Press (light weight) 3 × 15 reps Begin below 90° and progress
Lateral Raises 3 × 12 reps Thumbs up, scapular plane (30° forward of frontal)
Prone T/Y/W (with weights) 3 × 12 reps each Progress from 0 kg to 2–4 kg
TheraBand ER/IR (progressive) 3 × 20 reps Eccentric emphasis — tendon loading
Push-up (modified → full) 3 × 15 reps Controlled, full scapular motion
Pull-down (lat pulldown) 3 × 12 reps Wide grip, engage lats and posterior cuff
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full ROM
• ER strength >70% uninvolved
• Functional overhead reach pain-free
Phase 4 — Return to Full Activity (Month 6–12)
🎯 GOALS
• Full strength symmetry
• Return to sport / heavy work
• Overhead sport clearance
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 40
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Throwing athletes: structured return-to-throw program
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Progressive Overhead Loading 4 × 10 reps Sport/work-specific movements
Return-to-Throw Program (athletes)
Structured stages 30 ft → 60 ft → 90 ft → full throw
Sport-Specific Training Full sessions Swimming, throwing, racquet sports — progressive
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Isokinetic strength ≥90% symmetry
• No pain with full demand
• Surgeon clearance
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Thigpen CA et al. (2016). The American Society of Shoulder and Elbow Therapists' consensus statement on rehabilitation following arthroscopic rotator cuff repair. JSES.
• Millett PJ et al. (2006). Outcome of rotator cuff repair in athletes: return to sport. AOSSM.
• Koo SS & Burkhart SS. (2010). Rehabilitation following arthroscopic rotator cuff repair. Clin Sports Med.
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 41
10. Shoulder Impingement Syndrome Phase 1 — Pain Reduction (Week 0–3)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce subacromial inflammation
• Improve scapular positioning
• Pain ≤3/10
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid overhead reaching
• No painful arc activities
• Correct posture deficits
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pendulums 3 × 2 min Gentle distraction — reduce subacromial pressure
Scapular Retraction (sitting) 3 × 20 reps, 5 sec hold
Pull shoulder blades together and down
Chin Tucks 3 × 20 reps Correct forward head — affects scapular position
ER with band (low resistance) 3 × 20 reps Elbow at side — infraspinatus and teres minor
Posture correction exercises Hourly reminders Thoracic extension — key modifiable factor
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain ≤3/10 with daily activities
• Scapular resting position improved
Phase 2 — Strengthening (Week 3–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Rotator cuff and scapular stabiliser strength
• Full pain-free ROM
• Normal overhead mechanics
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Keep exercises in pain-free range
• Avoid empty can if painful — use full can position
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Full Can Exercise 3 × 15 reps Thumbs up, scapular plane — less subacromial stress than empty can
Side-lying ER 3 × 15 reps No compensation — pure ER movement
Prone Y/T/W 3 × 12 reps each Lower and mid trapezius — scapular upward rotation
Push-up Plus 3 × 15 reps Serratus anterior activation at end range
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 42
Cable Row 3 × 15 reps Retract and depress scapula at end range
Shoulder Flexion (below 90°) 3 × 15 reps Progress ROM as symptoms allow
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full overhead ROM pain-free
• Strength symmetry ≥80%
Phase 3 — Functional Return (Week 8–16)
🎯 GOALS
• Full sport or work return
• Overhead strength and endurance
• Self-management strategies
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Manage training load — avoid spikes
• Continue maintenance strengthening
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Overhead Press (progressive) 4 × 10 reps Progress from below to above 90°
Pull-ups / Lat Pulldown 4 × 8 reps Full range, control scapular movement
Sport/Work-Specific Loading Progressive sessions Mirror demands of the specific activity
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Symmetrical shoulder function
• Return to sport/occupation pain-free

11. Frozen Shoulder (Adhesive Capsulitis) Phase 1 — Painful / Freezing (Month 0–9)
🎯 GOALS
• Pain management
• Maintain available ROM
• Prevent further stiffness
• Education
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid aggressive stretching in painful phase — worsens symptoms
• Corticosteroid injection may be indicated
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pendulums 3 × 3 min all directions Pain relief and gentle distraction — key exercise
AAROM Flexion (cane) 3 × 15 reps Good arm assists — go to comfortable range only
ER Stretching (gentle) 3 × 30 sec Elbow at side, cane-assisted — no forcing
Heat before exercise 10 min Reduce viscosity of synovial fluid — improve ROM
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain stability (not pain resolution)
• Maintaining available ROM
Phase 2 — Stiffness / Frozen (Month 3–12)
🎯 GOALS
• Progressively restore ROM
• Pain reducing
• Restore function for ADL
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Progressive stretching appropriate now pain reducing
• Gentle but consistent pressure
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Capsular Stretching (ER, IR, flexion)
3 × 60 sec each direction
End-range hold, gentle over-pressure — consistent daily
Sleeper Stretch (posterior capsule)
3 × 45 sec Key for posterior capsule tightness
Cross-body Stretch 3 × 45 sec Horizontal adduction — posterior capsule
Pulleys 3 × 20 reps Aggressive ROM — daily consistency is key
Strengthening (pain-free range) 3 × 15 reps Band ER/IR, scapular exercises
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 44
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Gaining ROM weekly
• Flexion >150°
• Functional daily activities improving
Phase 3 — Thawing (Month 12–18+)
🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM restoration
• Full strength return
• Occupational/sport return
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• ROM may not fully return to pre-injury — educate patient
• Continued maintenance stretching
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Full ROM Stretching Program Daily 2 × sessions All capsular directions — maintain gains
Progressive Strengthening 4 × 10 reps All planes, progressive loading
Functional Overhead Training 3 × 15 reps Work/sport-specific overhead movements
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full or near-full ROM
• Symmetrical strength
• Full functional return
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Kelley MJ et al. (2013). Shoulder pain and mobility deficits: Adhesive capsulitis. Clinical Practice Guidelines. JOSPT.
• Hanchard NC et al. (2011). Conservative management following closed manipulation under anaesthesia for frozen shoulder. Cochrane.
• Rangan A et al. (2015). Management of adults with primary frozen shoulder in secondary care (UK FROST). Lancet.

12. Anterior Shoulder Dislocation (First-time) Phase 1 — Immobilisation (Week 0–3)
🎯 GOALS
• Tissue healing
• Pain & swelling management
• Maintain distal function
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Sling immobilisation 2–3 weeks
• Avoid ER and extension
• No overhead movements
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale

Wrist and hand strengthening 3 × 20 reps Grip strength — prevent distal atrophy
Pendulums (pain-free only) 2 × 2 min Gentle — after 1 week if comfortable
Isometric Rotator Cuff (submaximal)
3 × 10 reps, 5 sec hold
Maintain cuff activation without stress
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain settling
• Week 3 sling removal clearance

🎯 GOALS
• Full ROM (avoid combined ER + abduction initially)
• Rotator cuff strengthening
• Neuromuscular control
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid apprehension position (90° abduction + ER) for 8 weeks
• No throwing or overhead sport
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
AROM Flexion & Abduction 3 × 15 reps Progress range weekly in pain-free range
ER/IR Band Exercises 3 × 20 reps Elbow at side — avoid impingement position
Prone Y/T/W 3 × 15 reps Scapular stabiliser strengthening
Push-up Plus (wall) 3 × 20 reps Serratus anterior — dynamic stabiliser
Side-lying ER 3 × 15 reps Infraspinatus and teres minor — key posterior cuff
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full ROM achieved
• No apprehension with daily movements
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 46
• Good rotator cuff strength
Phase 3 — Return to Sport (Week 8–16)
🎯 GOALS
• Sport-specific overhead tolerance
• Strength symmetry
• Dynamic stability in all positions
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Return to contact sport with physio and surgeon clearance
• Educate re-dislocation risk
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Progressive ER loading in abduction
3 × 15 reps Gradually introduce apprehension position with control
Overhead Press 4 × 10 reps Full range when confident
Throwing Progression (athletes) Stage-by-stage program
30 ft → 60 ft → full velocity
Sport-Specific Training Full sessions Tackle situations, contact, overhead sport demands
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Confidence restored
• No apprehension in functional positions
• Strength symmetry
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Owens BD et al. (2011). Recurrence of glenohumeral instability: Am J Sports Med.

31. Biceps Tendinopathy (Long Head) Phase 1 — Acute / Protection
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce pain and inflammation in Biceps Tendinopathy (Long Head)
• Protect injured structure
• Maintain adjacent joint mobility
• Patient education
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid aggravating movements
• Respect tissue healing timeline
• Monitor for worsening or red flags
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Isometric Activation (primary muscle group)
3 × 10 reps, 5–10 sec hold
Sub-maximal — maintain activation without loading injured tissue
Adjacent Joint ROM 3 × 20 reps Maintain mobility in joints proximal and distal to injury
Gentle Aerobic Conditioning (pain-free mode)
20 min Bike, pool, or arm ergometer — based on injury site
Cryotherapy / Compression 15–20 min × 3–4/day Oedema and pain management
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain ≤3/10 at rest
• Swelling resolving
• Ready for progressive loading
Phase 2 — Subacute Strengthening
🎯 GOALS
• Progressive tissue loading
• Restore strength and ROM
• Normalise movement patterns
• Functional ADL independence
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor 24h pain response
• Avoid compensatory movement patterns
• Progress load based on symptom response
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Resistance Training (primary muscles)
3 × 15 reps (light to moderate)
Concentric/eccentric loading — progress weekly
Neuromuscular Control Exercises 3 × 20–30 sec Balance and proprioception — single-leg or single-arm
Functional Movement Training 3 × 12 reps Squat, hinge, push, pull — based on injury region
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 50
Flexibility / Mobility Work 3 × 45 sec Address identified mobility deficits contributing to injury
Cardiovascular Conditioning 30 min Progressively increase intensity toward pre-injury level
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Strength ≥75% limb symmetry
• Full pain-free ROM
• Functional tasks independent
Phase 3 — Return to Sport / Full Activity
🎯 GOALS
• Full strength symmetry ≥90%
• Sport/work-specific demands met
• Prevention education
• Self-management strategies
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• 10% weekly load increase rule
• Maintain long-term exercise program
• Re-injury risk counselling
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Sport/Work-Specific Drills Progressive sessions Mirror demands of target activity
Plyometrics / Power Training 3 × 10 reps Bilateral → unilateral progression
Agility & Change of Direction 4 sets Speed progression — reactive cues added
Strength Maintenance Program 2–3 × per week Maintain gains to prevent recurrence
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Functional tests ≥90% symmetry
• Psychological readiness confirmed
• Return to full unrestricted activity

ANKLE & FOOT 13. Lateral Ankle Sprain (Grade I-II) Phase 1 — PEACE (Day 0–3)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce swelling and pain
• Protect injured ligaments
• Begin early weight bearing
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• PEACE protocol: Protect, Elevate, Avoid anti-inflammatories, Compress, Educate
• No passive stretching in first 72h
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Ankle Pumps 10 reps every hour Reduce swelling — start immediately
Toe Curls / Marble pickups 3 × 20 reps Intrinsic foot muscle activation
RICE 20 min every 2h Elevate above heart level
Partial Weight Bearing (crutches if needed)
As tolerated Pain-free loading is better than rest
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Swelling reducing
• Pain ≤4/10 with WB
• Ready for LOVE phase
Phase 2 — LOVE & Early Rehab (Day 3–Week 4)
🎯 GOALS
• FWB pain-free
• Restore ROM
• Begin proprioception training
• Normal gait
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Brace or taping for support
• Avoid inversion loading
• Pain guide
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Calf Raises (bilateral) 3 × 20 reps Full ROM, slow and controlled
Resistance Band Eversion 3 × 20 reps Peroneal strengthening — critical for lateral stability
Alphabet Tracing (AROM) 2 × each letter Full ankle ROM in all planes
Single-leg Balance 3 × 30 sec Proprioception — eyes open then closed
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 60
Heel-Toe Walking 3 × 15 m Gait retraining
Stationary Bike 20 min Cardiovascular conditioning, ROM
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• FWB pain-free
• Normal gait
• Good balance on involved side
Phase 3 — Strength & Sport Return (Week 4–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Full strength
• Sport-specific agility
• Hop tests symmetry
• Return to sport
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• External support for 6 months for sport
• Monitor for re-sprain
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Calf Raises 4 × 15 reps Full ROM, progressive load — eccentric phase focus
Plyometric Hopping (bilateral then unilateral)
3 × 10 reps Sagittal then frontal then multi-directional
Lateral Band Walk 3 × 20 steps each Peroneal strength and functional stability
Agility Drills 4 sets Shuttle runs, T-drill, figure-8
Jump Rope 3 × 2 min Bilateral then unilateral — ankle loading
Sport-Specific Training Progressive return Cutting, pivoting, sport demands
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Single-leg hop symmetry ≥90%
• Balance ≤10% side difference
• Confident with sport demands
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Bleakley CM et al. (2012). PRICE needs updating, should we call the POLICE? BJSM.
• Gribble PA et al. (2016). Evidence review for the 2016 International Ankle Consortium consensus statement on the prevalence, impact and long-term consequences of lateral ankle sprains. BJSM.
• Vuurberg G et al. (2018). Diagnosis, treatment and prevention of ankle sprains: update of an evidence-based clinical guideline. BJSM.

14. Achilles Tendinopathy Phase 1 — Isometric Loading (Week 0–4)
🎯 GOALS
• Pain reduction
• Tendon loading tolerance
• Identify and modify contributing factors
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid stretching Achilles in reactive phase
• Modify training load
• Heel raise in shoe
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Isometric Calf Holds (knee straight)
5 × 45 sec, 70–80% effort
Standing calf raise held — immediate analgesic effect
Isometric Calf Holds (knee bent 30°)
5 × 45 sec Loads soleus predominantly
Bike / Swimming 30 min Maintain cardiovascular fitness without Achilles load
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain ≤4/10 during isometrics
• Morning stiffness <10 min
• VISA-A improving
Phase 2 — Heavy Slow Resistance (Week 4–8)
🎯 GOALS
• Tendon structural adaptation
• Strength — gastrocnemius and soleus
• Eccentric loading
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor 24h pain response — guide load
• Use pain monitoring model
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Double-leg Calf Raises (slow) 4 × 6 reps, 3-sec up / 4-sec down
Heavy slow resistance — gold standard for tendinopathy
Single-leg Eccentric Calf Drops 3 × 15 reps — knee straight
Gastrocnemius — Alfredson protocol adapted
Single-leg Eccentric Calf Drops (knee bent)
3 × 15 reps Soleus protocol — critical component
Seated Calf Raise (weight) 4 × 12 reps Isolate soleus — heavy loading
Hip and Glute Strengthening 3 × 15 reps Reduce Achilles load via proximal control
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 62
• VISA-A ≥60
• Heavy loading tolerated
• Morning stiffness minimal
Phase 3 — Energy Storage & Return to Run (Week 8–16)
🎯 GOALS
• Running tolerance
• Plyometric capacity
• Return to sport
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• 10% weekly mileage rule
• Avoid speed training until volume established
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pogo Hops (bilateral) 3 × 20 reps Rapid energy storage in tendon — fast elastic rebound
Single-leg Bounding 3 × 10 reps Eccentric + energy storage loading
Walk-Jog-Run Progression Stage program Start 1:2 walk:run ratio, progress weekly
Sport-Specific Drills Progressive sessions Cutting, jumping, acceleration/deceleration
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• VISA-A ≥80
• Running 30 min pain-free
• Sport demands met

15. Plantar Fasciitis Phase 1 — Acute Pain Management (Week 0–4)
🎯 GOALS
• Reduce morning pain
• Load management
• Intrinsic foot strengthening
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid barefoot walking on hard surfaces
• Night splint if severe morning pain
• Orthotic support
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Plantar Fascia Stretch (intrinsic) 3 × 30 sec each foot Pull toes back before stepping — pre-
activity
Calf Stretching (gastrocnemius) 3 × 45 sec each Knee straight — reduce tension on fascia
Towel / Marble Scrunches 3 × 20 reps Intrinsic foot strength — key long-term solution
Short Foot Exercise 3 × 20 reps, 5 sec hold
Arch activation — dome the foot without curling toes
Ice Massage 5–10 min Frozen water bottle rolling — post activity
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Morning pain <4/10
• First-step pain reducing
Phase 2 — Strengthening (Week 4–10)
🎯 GOALS
• Calf and intrinsic foot strength
• Load tolerance for walking
• Address contributing factors (hip, knee)
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• Progress load based on pain response
• Avoid barefoot plyometrics
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Calf Raises (single-leg, heavy) 4 × 15 reps — eccentric phase emphasis
Slow 4-sec lowering — loads plantar fascia progressively
Foot Doming 3 × 20 reps, hold 5 sec
Short foot — activates plantar intrinsics
Hip Abductor & Glute Strengthening
3 × 15 reps Reduces excessive pronation stress on fascia
Toe Spread & Control 3 × 20 reps Hallux and lesser toe control — foot stability
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app
Evidence-Based Rehab | 64
Step-ups 3 × 15 reps each Functional lower limb loading
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Walking 30 min pain-free
• Calf raise symmetrical
Phase 3 — Return to Running (Week 10–20)
🎯 GOALS
• Running tolerance
• Return to sport
• Long-term self-management
⚠ PRECAUTIONS
• No speed work until volume established
• Footwear review
• Maintain strengthening long-term
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Walk-Run Progression Stage program Start 1:3 walk:run, progress every 2 weeks
Plyometric Hopping 3 × 10 reps Bilateral first — monitor plantar fascia response
Running Gait Retraining If indicated Increase cadence 5–10% to reduce load
✅ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Running 30 min pain-free
• Morning pain <2/10
• Return to sport
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE • Beeson P. (2014). Plantar fasciopathy: revisiting the risk factors. Foot Ankle Surg.
• Rathleff MS et al. (2015). High-load strength training improves outcome in patients with plantar fasciitis. Scand J Med Sci Sports.

16. Ankle Fracture (Post-immobilisation) Phase 1 — Post-Cast Restoration (Week 0–4 post-cast)
🎯 GOALS
• Restore ankle ROM
• Reduce oedema
• Begin WB progression
• Gait retraining

• Follow surgeon WB status
• Monitor wound if ORIF

Ankle ROM (AROM all planes) 3 × 20 reps each direction
Alphabet tracing — restore dorsiflexion priority

• Calf and peroneal strength
• Normal gait without device
• Stairs

• No running until full WB and ROM

Calf Raises (standing bilateral) 3 × 20 reps Full range — toe raise focus
Peroneal Strengthening (band eversion)
3 × 20 reps Lateral stability restoration
Single-leg Balance 3 × 30 sec Proprioception retraining — progress surface
Step-ups and Step-downs 3 × 15 reps Functional loading — eccentric control

• Running
• Full sport return

• X-ray confirmed healing before high-impact

54.
Peroneal Tendinopathy
Phase 1 — Isometric Loading & Load Reduction (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce lateral ankle and peroneal pain
• Tendon loading via isometrics — analgesic effect
• Identify and modify provocative activities
• Patient education on tendon continuum model
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid stretching peroneal tendons in reactive
phase
• Reduce running mileage by 50%
• Avoid inversion stress loading
• Monitor for subluxation (snap over fibula)
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Isometric Eversion (band, mid-range) 5 × 45 sec, 70–80% effort Foot on floor, push outward against fixed
band — immediate analgesic effect
Isometric Plantarflexion (wall) 5 × 45 sec Maintain tendon activation without
provoking pain
Single-leg Balance (stable surface) 3 × 45 sec Proprioceptive loading with minimal tendon
stress
Bike / Swimming 20–30 min Maintain cardiovascular fitness — low
peroneal load
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £3/10 during isometrics
• Morning stiffness <15 min
• VISA-P (adapted) score improving
Phase 2 — Heavy Slow Resistance (Week 4–10)
n GOALS
• Tendon structural adaptation via progressive
loading
• Peroneus longus and brevis strength symmetry
• Restore normal ankle biomechanics
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid plyometrics and sprinting
• Apply 24h pain rule — guide load progression
• Monitor for tendon subluxation with loading
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Eversion with Resistance Band (slow tempo) 4 × 12 reps, 3-sec
concentric / 4-sec eccentric
Heavy slow resistance protocol — gold
standard for tendinopathy
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 7
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Calf Raises (eversion bias) 4 × 12 reps, slow eccentric Roll off the lateral border of foot at top —
loads peroneus longus
Resisted Plantarflexion/Eversion (Theraband) 3 × 15 reps Combined motion — functional peroneal
loading pattern
Step-up with Lateral Load 3 × 12 reps each Functional closed chain peroneal activation
Single-leg Balance (foam) 3 × 45 sec Proprioception progression — unstable
surface
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Heavy loading tolerated without 24h pain spike
• Eversion strength >75% symmetry
• Ready for plyometric introduction
Phase 3 — Return to Sport (Week 10–20)
n GOALS
• Full plyometric and cutting tolerance
• Sport-specific ankle loading
• Eversion strength symmetry ³90%
• Full return to running and sport
n PRECAUTIONS
• 10% weekly mileage increase rule
• Maintain lateral ankle brace for first 4–6 weeks of
sport return
• Monitor for recurrence of snap/subluxation
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Lateral Bounds (bilateral ® unilateral) 3 × 10 reps each Energy storage loading — land softly with
peroneal control
Agility Ladder (lateral patterns) 3 × 4 sets Reactive ankle loading in multiple planes
Walk-Jog-Run Progression Stage program Begin week 10 if strength criteria met —
straight then curves
Sport-Specific Cutting and Pivoting Progressive sessions Controlled introduction of
change-of-direction loads
Strength Maintenance Program 2–3 × per week Maintain eccentric peroneal strength to
prevent recurrence
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Hop test LSI ³90%
• Running 30 min pain-free
• Sport-specific demands met without pain
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE
• Dombek MF et al. (2003). Peroneal tendon tears: a retrospective review. J Foot Ankle Surg.
• Roster B et al. (2016). Peroneal tendon tears with and without ankle instability. Foot Ankle Int.

55.
Posterior Tibial Tendon Dysfunction (PTTD)
Phase 1 — Acute / Offloading (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce pain and inflammation along medial
ankle
• Support arch via orthotic or CAM boot (Stage II)
• Maintain tibialis posterior activation without
overload
• Patient education on flatfoot progression
n PRECAUTIONS
• Stage II+: CAM boot or UCBL orthosis for 4–6
weeks
• Avoid barefoot walking on hard surfaces
• No heel raises on affected side in reactive phase
• Monitor for worsening arch collapse (too far
lateral heel)
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Isometric Tibialis Posterior (arch doming) 3 × 10 reps, 10 sec hold Short foot exercise — dome arch without
curling toes, sub-maximal
Seated Calf Raises (bilateral) 3 × 20 reps Low load — avoid full single-leg load in
acute phase
Ankle Pumps & AROM 3 × 20 reps each Maintain ankle mobility and reduce oedema
Pool Walking / Hydrotherapy 20 min Offloaded functional walking — excellent
early option
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £3/10 with weight bearing
• Swelling resolving
• Ready for progressive loading
Phase 2 — Progressive Strengthening (Week 4–12)
n GOALS
• Restore tibialis posterior strength and endurance
• Single-leg heel raise symmetry
• Normalise gait mechanics
• Reduce arch collapse with functional tasks
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid plyometrics and high-impact running
• Continue orthotic support during loading
• Monitor 24h pain response after each session
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Heel Raise (eccentric focus) 4 × 15 reps, slow 4-sec
lowering
Eccentric tibialis posterior loading — key
intervention for PTTD
Tibialis Posterior Resistance (band) 3 × 20 reps Inversion + plantarflexion combined —
mirrors function of TP

physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 10
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Short Foot / Arch Doming 3 × 20 reps, 5 sec hold Activate intrinsic foot muscles — support
medial longitudinal arch
Step-up with Arch Control 3 × 15 reps each Functional loading with cue to maintain arch
height
Single-leg Balance (arch awareness) 3 × 45 sec Maintain arch position — progress to
foam/unstable surface
Hip Abductor & Glute Strengthening 3 × 15 reps Reduce tibial internal rotation — reduce TP
tendon stress
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• 10 single-leg heel raises without pain
• Arch maintains height with single-leg stance
• Normal gait on flat surfaces
Phase 3 — Return to Full Activity (Week 12–24)
n GOALS
• Full single-leg calf raise symmetry (³25 reps)
• Return to running and sport
• Long-term arch support and self-management
n PRECAUTIONS
• Continued orthotic use for 12+ months
post-rehab
• Avoid barefoot sport on hard surfaces long-term
• Re-assess for surgical referral if Stage III–IV
(rigid flatfoot)
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Calf Raises (progressive load) 4 × 20 reps Add backpack weight when bodyweight
tolerated — symmetry goal
Walk-Run Progression Stage program, 10%
weekly
Begin when 20 single-leg raises pain-free
Plyometric Hopping (sagittal then frontal) 3 × 10 reps Bilateral first — monitor arch and pain
response
Sport-Specific Drills Progressive sessions Cutting, pivoting — with orthotic support
Strength Maintenance 2–3 × per week Eccentric heel raises lifelong to prevent
recurrence
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Single-leg heel raise ³25 reps without pain
• Running 30 min pain-free
• Full sport participation without arch pain
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE
• Myerson MS. (1997). Adult acquired flatfoot deformity. J Bone Joint Surg.

56.
Sinus Tarsi Syndrome
Phase 1 — Pain Reduction & Protection (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce pain in lateral hindfoot (sinus tarsi region)
• Control subtalar joint irritation
• Protect ligamentous structures
• Patient education — often post-ankle sprain
sequela
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid inversion loading and uneven terrain
• Lateral wedge orthosis or taping to reduce
subtalar stress
• No running until pain £3/10 with walking
• Consider corticosteroid injection if conservative
measures fail at 6 weeks
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Ankle AROM (pain-free range) 3 × 20 reps each direction Dorsiflex, plantarflex, eversion — avoid
forced inversion
Intrinsic Foot Strengthening (towel scrunches) 3 × 20 reps Maintain foot muscle activation while
offloading subtalar joint
Single-leg Balance (stable) 3 × 30 sec Proprioceptive activation — avoid inversion
wobble
Cryotherapy / Compression 15 min × 3–4/day Sinus tarsi oedema and inflammation
management
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £3/10 with walking on flat surface
• Swelling in sinus tarsi region reducing
• Ready for progressive loading
Phase 2 — Strengthening (Week 4–10)
n GOALS
• Restore peroneal and tibialis posterior strength
• Improve subtalar and midfoot stability
• Normalise gait mechanics
• Proprioception restoration
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid deep inversion stretches
• Progress surfaces gradually — monitor subtalar
pain
• Use taping/brace for sport activities
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Peroneal Eversion (band) 3 × 20 reps Lateral stabiliser strengthening — key for
subtalar control
Calf Raises (bilateral then unilateral) 3 × 20 reps Full ROM — maintain subtalar neutral
position
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 13
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Short Foot / Arch Doming 3 × 20 reps Intrinsic support for midtarsal stability
Single-leg Balance (foam pad) 3 × 45 sec Subtalar proprioception — progress to
perturbation
Step-up and Step-down 3 × 15 reps each Functional closed chain loading in
controlled range
Hip and Glute Strengthening 3 × 15 reps Reduce excessive pronation forces through
the subtalar joint
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Walking 30 min pain-free
• Single-leg balance ³45 sec on foam
• Normal gait without pain on stairs
Phase 3 — Return to Activity (Week 10–20)
n GOALS
• Return to running and sport
• Full confidence on uneven terrain
• Long-term recurrence prevention
n PRECAUTIONS
• Maintain orthotic support for running long-term
• Gradual return to trail/uneven terrain
• 10% weekly mileage rule

post-symptom onset

57.
5th Metatarsal Fracture (Jones Fracture)
Phase 1 — Protection / Immobilisation (Week 0–6)
n GOALS
• Protect zone II fracture healing (poor blood
supply region)
• NWB or TTWB per surgeon protocol
• Maintain proximal fitness and strength
• DVT prevention
n PRECAUTIONS
• NWB mandatory — Jones fracture has high
non-union risk
• CAM boot or short-leg cast per surgeon
• No inversion or lateral foot loading
• Surgical fixation may be indicated in athletes —
follow post-op protocol
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Ankle Pumps & AROM (pain-free) 10 × every hour DVT prevention — within boot if allowed by
surgeon
Upper Body & Core Conditioning As tolerated Maintain general fitness — seated rowing,
upper body weights
Stationary Bike (unaffected leg) 20 min Cardiovascular maintenance — no foot
loading
Hip Strengthening (side-lying) 3 × 20 reps Prevent deconditioning — maintain proximal
strength
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Radiographic evidence of healing (week 6–8 X-ray)
• Surgeon clearance for weight bearing
• Pain £3/10 at rest
Phase 2 — Progressive Weight Bearing (Week 6–12)
n GOALS
• FWB progression over 2–4 weeks
• Restore ankle and foot ROM
• Calf and peroneal strengthening
• Normalise gait pattern
n PRECAUTIONS
• Progress WB based on pain AND radiographic
healing
• Avoid barefoot walking until full FWB in shoes
• Monitor for refracture — use lateral support
footwear
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pool Walking (aquatic WB) 20 min Offloaded weight bearing — begin when
permitted
Ankle AROM (all planes) 3 × 20 reps each Restore dorsiflexion, plantarflexion,
eversion — avoid forced inversion
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 15
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Bilateral Calf Raises 3 × 20 reps Begin when FWB pain-free — progress
weight bearing through forefoot
Peroneal Strengthening (band) 3 × 20 reps Restore lateral foot stabilisers — protect
zone II
Single-leg Balance (stable) 3 × 30 sec Proprioception restoration — when FWB
tolerated
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• FWB in shoe without pain
• Full ankle ROM restored
• Radiographic healing confirmed
Phase 3 — Return to Activity (Week 12–20)
n GOALS
• Return to running and sport
• Full foot strength symmetry
• Hop test symmetry ³90%
n PRECAUTIONS
• No sprint or plyometric loading until 12 weeks
minimum
• Athlete return to sport may require 16–20 weeks
• Consider carbon fibre plate insole for 6 months
post-return
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Single-leg Calf Raises 4 × 15 reps Full ROM eccentric emphasis — symmetry
target before running
Walk-Run Progression Stage program Begin week 12 with surgeon clearance —
flat surface, 10% weekly
Lateral Band Walks 3 × 20 steps Peroneal and lateral foot stability — protect
refracture zone
Plyometric Hopping (bilateral ® unilateral) 3 × 10 reps Bilateral first — monitor lateral foot pain
response
Sport-Specific Drills Progressive sessions Cutting, pivoting — with carbon fibre plate
insole support
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Hop test LSI ³90%
• Running 30 min pain-free
• Radiographic union confirmed

Phase 1 — Protection (Week 0–6)
n GOALS
• Wound healing and oedema management
• NWB per surgeon protocol
• Prevent DVT
• Maintain proximal strength and cardiovascular
fitness
n PRECAUTIONS
• Strict NWB unless surgeon permits TTWB
• Monitor wound for signs of infection
• No ankle ROM exercises until surgeon clearance
(typically week 2)
• Anticoagulation per medical team — DVT risk
high
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Ankle Pumps (within boot) 10 reps every hour Immediate post-op — DVT prevention and

NWB

maintain fitness

NWB phase
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Wound healed, sutures removed
• Surgeon clearance for PWB/FWB at 6-week review
• Pain £3/10 at rest

n GOALS
• FWB progression over 2–4 weeks
• Restore ankle ROM — dorsiflexion priority
• Calf and peroneal strength
• Normalise gait pattern without assistive device
n PRECAUTIONS

advance without clearance
• No inversion if fibula ORIF — avoid lateral stress
• Monitor hardware for discomfort with loading

Ankle AROM — all planes 3 × 20 reps each Alphabet tracing — restore dorsiflexion as
priority to normalise gait

FWB on land

• No running or high-impact until ROM and

Tibialis Anterior Tendinopathy
Phase 1 — Isometric Loading & Load Management (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce anterior ankle pain along tibialis anterior
tendon
• Isometric loading for immediate analgesia
• Identify and modify training provocations
• Footwear assessment — tongue pressure
management
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid stretching tibialis anterior in reactive phase
• Modify footwear — lace technique to relieve
tongue pressure
• Reduce downhill running and stairs loading
• Monitor for anterior compartment syndrome if
acute onset with swelling
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Isometric Dorsiflexion (foot against wall) 5 × 45 sec, 70–80% effort Immediate analgesic effect — key first-line
exercise
Isometric Inversion (foot against fixed surface) 5 × 45 sec Combined tibialis anterior function —
inversion + dorsiflexion
Bike / Swimming 20–30 min Cardiovascular maintenance with minimal
TA loading
Calf Stretching (gastrocnemius) 3 × 45 sec Improve dorsiflexion range — reduce TA
compensatory overload
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £3/10 during isometrics
• Morning stiffness <15 min
• Footwear modification implemented
Phase 2 — Heavy Slow Resistance (Week 4–10)
n GOALS
• Tibialis anterior structural adaptation
• Dorsiflexion strength symmetry
• Restore normal ankle biomechanics
n PRECAUTIONS
• Monitor 24h pain response after each loading
session
• Avoid plyometrics and impact loading
• Progress load weekly — do not rush to heavy
resistance
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Resisted Dorsiflexion (band, slow tempo) 4 × 12 reps, 3-sec up /
4-sec down
Heavy slow resistance — 3-sec concentric,
4-sec eccentric lowering
Resisted Inversion (band) 4 × 12 reps, slow tempo Combined function loading — mirrors tibialis
anterior action

Non-specific Low Back Pain (Acute)
Phase 1 — Acute Pain Management (Week 0–2)
n GOALS
• Reduce pain and muscle guarding
• Maintain mobility and avoid deconditioning
• Patient education — reassurance and
self-management
• Identify and address yellow flags (fear-avoidance,
catastrophising)
n PRECAUTIONS
• Screen for red flags: cauda equina, fracture,
malignancy
• Avoid prolonged bed rest — stay active within
pain tolerance
• No heavy lifting or sustained flexion loading
• NSAIDs may be prescribed — not a substitute for
movement
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Walking (paced, flat surface) 10–20 min × 2/day Best evidence for acute LBP — maintain
normal spinal loading
Knee-to-Chest Stretch (lumbar flexion) 3 × 30 sec each Gentle lumbar flexion mobilisation —
symptom-guide
Cat-Camel (lumbar flexion/extension) 3 × 10 reps Segmental lumbar mobility — promotes
synovial fluid circulation
Prone Lying (extension bias if centralising) 3 × 5 min McKenzie extension if pain peripheralises
with flexion
Diaphragmatic Breathing 5 min × 3/day Reduce sympathetic nervous system
activation — pain modulation
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £4/10 with daily activities
• Able to walk 20 min without significant pain increase
• Red flags excluded
• Ready for progressive strengthening

Phase 2 — Motor Control & Strengthening (Week 2–8)
n GOALS
• Restore lumbopelvic motor control
• Core muscle endurance (not just strength)
• Normalise movement patterns
• Return to full daily activities
n PRECAUTIONS
• Pain should not exceed 4/10 during exercise
• Avoid high-load spinal flexion (deadlift) in early
phase
• Progress gradually — flare-ups are common and
manageable

Dead Bug (contralateral arm/leg) 3 × 10 reps each side Deep abdominal + transversus abdominis

Hip Flexor Stretch 3 × 45 sec each Reduce anterior pelvic tilt — reduce lumbar

Walking Program (progressive) 30 min daily Best evidence intervention for LBP —
graded increase
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £2/10 with all ADLs
• Motor control restored — consistent neutral spine in functional tasks
• Full daily activities independent
• Ready for return to work / sport loading

n GOALS
• Return to work, sport, and recreational activities
• Load tolerance for bending, lifting, and twisting
• Long-term recurrence prevention
• Self-management independence
n PRECAUTIONS
• Recurrence rate is high (50–80% within 1 year)
— maintain program
• Address occupational risk factors
• 10% weekly load increase rule for sport return

Romanian Deadlift (hip hinge) 4 × 10 reps Teach hip-dominant lifting pattern — protect
lumbar spine

Lumbar Disc Herniation with Radiculopathy
Phase 1 — Acute Radicular Pain Management (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce radicular pain and neurological
symptoms
• Centralisation of symptoms (directional
preference)
• Patient education — natural history is favourable
• Maintain mobility and prevent deconditioning
n PRECAUTIONS
• URGENT: Cauda equina (bilateral leg weakness,
bowel/bladder dysfunction) — emergency referral
• Progressive neurological deficit requires urgent
surgical review
• Avoid sustained lumbar flexion — worsens disc
prolapse
• NSAIDs + physiotherapy combined are more
effective than either alone
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Prone Lying / Press-ups (extension) 3 × 10 reps / 3 × 5 min McKenzie extension — centralise leg
symptoms; only if symptoms centralise
Walking (short, frequent bouts) 10 min × 3–4/day Avoid sustained sitting — intermittent
loading best
Neural Mobilisation (sciatic nerve slider) 3 × 10 reps each Ankle DF/PF with straight leg — gentle
nerve gliding, NOT if acute
Lumbar Traction (if clinically indicated) Per physiotherapist Intermittent mechanical traction — evidence
modest but may help selected patients
Sleeping Posture Education Daily cue Side-lying with pillow between knees —
reduce disc pressure
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Symptoms centralising (leg pain reducing, back pain may increase — acceptable)
• Pain £4/10 with walking
• No progressive neurological deficit
Phase 2 — Stabilisation & Strengthening (Week 4–12)
n GOALS
• Lumbopelvic stabilisation
• Nerve root pain resolved or significantly reduced
• Restore full lumbar ROM
• Return to full daily activities
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid heavy axial spinal loading (heavy deadlifts)
before 12 weeks
• Avoid prolonged sitting >30 min without
movement break
• Monitor for symptom recurrence with loading

Cervical Radiculopathy
Phase 1 — Acute Nerve Root Management (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce arm pain and neurological symptoms
• Centralise symptoms (neck pain preferred over

n PRECAUTIONS
• URGENT: Myelopathy signs (bilateral symptoms,

• Progressive motor weakness — urgent imaging
• No cervical manipulation in acute nerve root

symptom relief

Spondylolisthesis (Grade I–II, Conservative)
Phase 1 — Pain Management & Education (Week 0–6)
n GOALS
• Reduce lumbar and referred leg pain
• Educate patient — Grade I–II rarely requires
surgery
• Identify and manage activity-related provocations
• Establish neutral spine awareness
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid end-range lumbar extension (worsens
spondylolysis/listhesis)
• No contact sport or high-impact activity in acute
phase
• Monitor for neurological symptoms — cauda
equina is red flag
• Lumbar brace may reduce pain in acute phase
(6–8 weeks)
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pelvic Tilt (posterior tilt to neutral) 3 × 20 reps Reduce lumbar lordosis — reduces anterior
shear force at slip level
Dead Bug (modified — knees only) 3 × 10 reps Maintain neutral pelvis throughout — avoid
lumbar extension
Bridge (isometric hold) 3 × 15 reps, 5 sec hold Posterior chain activation in neutral spine
position
Walking (paced, flat surface) 20–30 min daily Low-impact loading — maintain fitness
without provocative forces
Hip Flexor Stretch 3 × 45 sec each Tight hip flexors increase anterior pelvic tilt
— worsen listhesis stress
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £3/10 with daily activities
• Neutral spine position achieved in lying and sitting
• No worsening neurological symptoms
Phase 2 — Core Stabilisation (Week 6–16)
n GOALS
• Lumbar stabiliser strength and endurance
• Restore functional movement patterns in neutral
spine
• Return to full daily activities and work
• Begin graduated sport/recreational loading
n PRECAUTIONS
• Continue to avoid lumbar end-range extension
loading
• No return to extension-loading sport (gymnastics,
cricket fast bowling, swimming butterfly) until
Phase 3
• Monitor for increase in slip with heavy loading

physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 36
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Dead Bug (full progression) 3 × 10 reps each Contralateral arm/leg extension —
transversus abdominis co-activation
Bird Dog (progression to loaded) 3 × 10 reps each Maintain neutral lumbar spine — do NOT
allow extension
Side Plank (progression) 3 × 30–45 sec each Lateral core — reduce rotational and lateral
shear
Prone Plank 3 × 30–45 sec Global core endurance — key for spinal
stability
Hip Strengthening Circuit 3 × 15 reps each Glute max, glute med, hamstrings — reduce
lumbopelvic stress
Step-ups and Split Squat 3 × 12 reps each Unilateral lower limb loading — neutral
spine maintained
Stationary Bike / Pool Walking 30 min Cardiovascular conditioning —
spine-friendly modalities
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain £1/10 with all ADLs
• Core endurance: plank ³60 sec, side plank ³45 sec
• Full daily function independent
Phase 3 — Return to Sport (Week 16–24+)
n GOALS
• Return to sport and full recreational activities
• Sport-specific loading tolerance
• Long-term spinal health maintenance
n PRECAUTIONS
• Extension-dominant sports require gradual
graded return
• Consider imaging review before contact or
high-impact sport return
• Long-term core maintenance program essential
— recurrence prevention
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Romanian Deadlift (hip hinge) 4 × 10 reps Hip-dominant loading — maintain neutral
lumbar throughout
Trap Bar Deadlift 4 × 10 reps Safer spinal loading than barbell deadlift —
reduced shear force
Leg Press 4 × 12 reps Axial loading in controlled spine-neutral
position
Pallof Press (anti-rotation) 3 × 12 reps each Rotational core stability for sport-specific
demands
Sport-Specific Return Program Progressive stages Gradual return — avoid high-impact until 6
months symptom-free
Core Maintenance Program 3 × per week lifelong Prevent deconditioning and recurrence —
non-negotiable long-term

n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Pain-free with all sport demands
• No neurological symptoms with loading
• Clinician and surgeon clearance for full return

SPINE & UPPER LIMB
29.
Thoracic Outlet Syndrome (TOS)
Phase 1 — Symptom Control & Neural Offloading (Week 0–4)
n GOALS
• Reduce arm pain, paraesthesia, and neurovascular
symptoms
• Identify TOS subtype: neurogenic (95%), venous, or
arterial
• Posture correction — address forward head and
rounded shoulders
• Patient education on provocative positions
n PRECAUTIONS
• Arterial TOS (limb ischaemia, pallor) — urgent
vascular referral
• Venous TOS (Paget-Schroetter: arm swelling,
cyanosis) — urgent thrombosis management
• Avoid overhead arm positions in early phase
• No cervical manipulation until TOS subtype
confirmed
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Cervical Retraction (chin tucks) 3 × 15 reps, 5 sec hold Correct forward head posture — reduces
scalene tension on brachial plexus
Scalene Stretch (lateral cervical flexion + rotation) 3 × 45 sec each Gentle lengthening of anterior and middle
scalene — do not provoke symptoms
Pectoralis Minor Stretch (doorway) 3 × 45 sec Key restriction in TOS — opens
costoclavicular space
Scapular Retraction + Depression 3 × 20 reps, 5 sec hold First rib depression via lower trapezius —
opens thoracic outlet
Diaphragmatic Breathing 5 min × 3/day Scalene muscles are accessory breathers
— reduce overuse via diaphragm retraining
Neural Mobilisation — Median/Ulnar Sliders 3 × 10 reps each Brachial plexus mobilisation — gentle
sliders in symptom-free range
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Arm symptoms reducing (pain, paraesthesia improving)
• Posture correction sustained in sitting
• Provocative tests (EAST, Roos) less positive
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 7
Phase 2 — Postural Strengthening & Neural Mobilisation (Week 4–12)
n GOALS
• Scapular stabiliser and deep cervical flexor strength
• First rib mobility restoration
• Full pain-free cervical and upper limb ROM
• Restore overhead tolerance
n PRECAUTIONS
• Avoid sustained overhead work until Phase 3
• Monitor for symptom increase with loading
• Ergonomic workstation modification — keyboard,
monitor height
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Deep Cervical Flexor Training (craniocervical
flexion)
3 × 10 reps, 10 sec hold Longus colli activation — reduces scalene
overload on brachial plexus
Prone Y/T/W 3 × 12 reps Lower and middle trapezius — scapular
depression and retraction
Serratus Anterior — Wall Slide 3 × 15 reps Upward scapular rotation — opens
costoclavicular space
First Rib Mobilisation (self) 3 × 10 reps Posterior depression of first rib via towel —
reduces scalene attachment tension
Thoracic Extension (foam roller) 3 × 10 reps Restore thoracic extension — reduces
compensatory cervical forward posture
Brachial Plexus Neural Tensioner (progressive) 3 × 10 reps Progress from slider to tensioner as
symptoms allow — maintain symptom
control
Shoulder ER/IR Band (below 90°) 3 × 20 reps Rotator cuff strength — maintain arm
function without provoking TOS
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Overhead reach to 120° without symptom provocation
• EAST test negative or minimally positive
• Scapular position corrected at rest
Phase 3 — Full Function & Return to Activity (Week 12–24)
n GOALS
• Full overhead strength and endurance
• Return to sport and occupational demands
• Long-term postural maintenance
n PRECAUTIONS
• Surgical referral (first rib resection, scalenectomy) if
no improvement at 3–6 months
• Avoid sustained overhead occupation without
ergonomic support
• Maintain strengthening program long-term —
recurrence common
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Overhead Press (progressive) 4 × 10 reps Begin below 90° — increase range weekly
as symptoms allow
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Page 8
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale
Pull-ups / Lat Pulldown 4 × 10 reps Scapular depression strength — opens
thoracic outlet with each rep
Sport-Specific Upper Body Loading Progressive sessions Throwing, swimming, racquet sport —
graded return program
Postural Maintenance Education Daily habit Workstation, sleep position, carrying habits
— long-term self-management
n CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE
• Full overhead sport/work demands met without provocation
• No arm paraesthesia or vascular symptoms
• Self-management program independent
REFERENCES & EVIDENCE BASE
• Hooper TL et al. (2010). Thoracic outlet syndrome: a controversial clinical condition. J Man Manip Ther.
• Povlsen B et al. (2014). Treatment for thoracic outlet syndrome. Cochrane Database Syst Rev.
• Kuhn JE et al. (2015). Thoracic outlet syndrome. J Am Acad Orthop Surg.
• Vanti C et al. (2007). Conservative treatment of thoracic outlet syndrome. Eur Med Phys.
