99. Thoracic Hyperkyphosis (Postural)
Phase 1 — Postural Education & Mobility (Week 0–4)
■ GOALS • Increase thoracic extension mobility • Reduce associated cervical and lumbar compensatory pain • Patient education on postural contributors: sitting habits, technology use, occupation • Establish postural awareness program
■ PRECAUTIONS • Differentiate postural from structural hyperkyphosis (Scheuermann's disease, osteoporotic fracture) • Scheuermann's: anterior wedging ≥5° in ≥3 adjacent vertebrae on X-ray — different management • Osteoporotic kyphosis in older adults: bone health assessment mandatory before loading • Screen for thoracic pain with neurological features — cord compression rare but serious • Flexibility goals may be limited in adults — focus on symptom reduction and prevention of worsening
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale Thoracic Extension over Foam Roller 3 × 10 reps, 30 sec pause Passive thoracic extension — target mid-thoracic apex of kyphosis Thoracic Extension over Chair Back 3 × 20 reps Accessible thoracic mobilisation — daily practice essential for change Cat-Camel (thoracic focus) 3 × 15 reps Segmental thoracic mobility — emphasise mid-thoracic extension range Chest Opener Stretch (doorway) 3 × 45 sec Pectoralis minor and major stretch — reverses protraction and kyphosis posture Cervical Retraction (chin tucks) 3 × 15 reps Correct forward head posture — coupled with thoracic extension Postural Awareness Training Hourly cue Set phone reminders — seated and standing postural correction throughout day
■ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE • Thoracic extension mobility improved (≥5° from baseline) • Cervical and upper back pain ≤3/10 • Postural correction sustained 50% of resting time • Ready for strengthening program
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app | Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Protocols 86–100
Phase 2 — Strengthening & Postural Control (Week 4–12)
■ GOALS • Scapular retractor and thoracic extensor strengthening • Reduce upper trapezius and pectoral dominance • Deep cervical flexor and core strengthening • Sustained postural improvement in functional positions
■ PRECAUTIONS • Avoid strengthening in kyphotic posture — reinforce poor alignment • Address ergonomic factors: screen height, chair, keyboard position • In adolescents with Scheuermann's: bracing (Milwaukee or TLSO) may be indicated — coordinate with spine specialist
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale Prone Y, T, W (scapular retractors) 3 × 12 reps Middle and lower trapezius — primary scapular retractor program Seated Row (cable or band) 4 × 15 reps Scapular retraction under load — functional strengthening with postural cue Face Pull (band or cable) 3 × 15 reps Rear deltoid and external rotators — correct protraction and IR dominance Thoracic Extension (prone, loaded progression) 3 × 15 reps Thoracic extensor strengthening — begin bodyweight, progress to loaded Deep Cervical Flexor Training 3 × 10 reps, 10 sec Longus colli — forward head posture correction Dead Bug (thoracic neutral) 3 × 10 reps each Core stabilisation with thoracic extension cue — anti-flexion training Wall Angels 3 × 15 reps Simultaneous shoulder ER + thoracic extension — excellent posture integrator Ergonomic Assessment & Modification One-off assessment Screen, chair, keyboard, mouse — structural solution for postural problem
■ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE • Scapular retractor strength ≥75% symmetry with rhomboids/mid-trap • Sustained neutral thoracic posture during all strengthening exercises • Daily activity posture improved (≥70% time in corrected posture) • Cervical and thoracic pain ≤1/10

100. Temporomandibular Joint Dysfunction (TMJ)
Phase 1 — Pain Reduction & Joint Protection (Week 0–4)
■ GOALS • Reduce TMJ pain, clicking, and jaw locking • Offload TMJ via dietary and behavioural modification • Identify and address parafunctional habits (bruxism, clenching) • Patient education on TMJ mechanics and self-management
■ PRECAUTIONS • Multidisciplinary: dentist (occlusal splint), physiotherapist, psychologist for bruxism and stress • Avoid: hard foods, large bites, prolonged gum chewing, jaw clenching, teeth grinding • Exclude: odontogenic infection, parotid pathology, rheumatoid arthritis, psoriatic arthritis (TMJ involvement) • Locking jaw with limited opening requires urgent dentist / oral maxillofacial referral • Cervical dysfunction is highly associated with TMD — always assess and treat cervical spine
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale Jaw Rest Protocol Ongoing Soft diet, small bites, no gum — reduce joint loading during reactive phase Occlusal Splint (dentist-provided) Night use (bruxism) Reduce nocturnal joint loading and clenching — primary TMD intervention Diaphragmatic Breathing 5 min × 3/day Reduce sympathetic nervous system activation — key driver of jaw clenching Thermal Therapy (moist heat) 10–15 min, 3×/day Reduce masseteric muscle tension — moist heat over masseter and TMJ Tongue-Up Rest Position Conscious habit all day Tongue on palate, teeth apart, lips together — reduces TMJ compression Relaxation Techniques / Stress Management Daily practice Stress is primary driver of bruxism and TMD — mindfulness, progressive relaxation
■ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE • Pain ≤3/10 with daily jaw use (eating, talking) • Jaw opening ≥35 mm without pain (goal ≥40 mm) • Morning jaw pain and stiffness reducing • Ready for progressive jaw exercise program
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app | Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Protocols 86–100
Phase 2 — Jaw Mobility & Muscle Re-education (Week 4–10)
■ GOALS • Restore full pain-free jaw opening (≥40 mm) • Restore lateral and protrusive jaw movements • Re-educate TMJ opening pattern — avoid lateral deviation • Address cervical dysfunction contributing to TMD
■ PRECAUTIONS • Avoid aggressive jaw stretching — risk of disc displacement or ligament strain • Pain should not exceed 3/10 during exercise — gentle, within pain-free range • Monitor for disc displacement (click then lock progression) — dentist referral if locking worsens
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale Controlled Jaw Opening (straight-line) 3 × 10 reps Mirror feedback — correct lateral deviation; maintain midline opening Jaw Opening with Tongue on Palate 3 × 10 reps, slow Limits condylar translation — reduces anterior disc loading in early opening Lateral Jaw Deviation (active, pain-free) 3 × 10 reps each direction Restore lateral pterygoid function — key for lateral jaw mobility Masseter and Temporalis Self-Massage 5 min, 2×/day Reduce hyperactive jaw closers — circular pressure at muscle belly Resisted Jaw Opening (gentle) 3 × 10 reps, 5 sec hold Lateral pterygoid strengthening — submaximal resistance under chin Cervical Spine Treatment Per physiotherapist Upper cervical manipulation or mobilisation — C1-C3 referral to TMJ is common Deep Cervical Flexor Training 3 × 10 reps, 10 sec Forward head posture correction — directly reduces masticatory muscle overload Postural Correction Program Ongoing Thoracic extension, chin tuck — reduce forward head posture TMJ loading
■ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE • Jaw opening ≥40 mm without pain • Lateral deviation ≤2 mm from midline • Clicking reducing or absent • Cervical ROM and dysfunction improved
Phase 3 — Long-Term Self-Management & Prevention (Week 10–24)
PhysioNutrition — MSK Rehab Protocols | physionutrition.vercel.app | Evidence-Based Rehab
physionutrition.vercel.app | Protocols 86–100
■ GOALS • Full pain-free jaw function for all ADLs (eating, speaking, yawning) • Long-term bruxism management program • Independence in self-management • Prevention of relapse with stress management
■ PRECAUTIONS • TMD has high recurrence rate with psychosocial stressors — ongoing stress management is mandatory • Annual dental review: occlusal splint adjustment as teeth shift • Contact sports: custom-fit mouthguard required — prevents direct TMJ trauma • Sleep hygiene optimisation — bruxism is NREM-associated; sleep quality directly affects severity
Exercise Parameters Clinical Cue / Rationale Daily Jaw Exercise Program (5 min) Daily, lifelong Controlled opening, lateral movements — maintain mobility permanently Stress Management / Mindfulness Daily practice Primary driver of recurrence — integrate mindfulness or CBT techniques Postural Maintenance Program 3 × per week Cervical and thoracic postural exercises — TMD-cervical link permanent Occlusal Splint Compliance Nightly, ongoing Maintain splint use during sleep indefinitely if bruxism persists Self-Monitoring Ongoing Awareness of daytime clenching habits — biofeedback app or timer reminders
■ CRITERIA TO PROGRESS TO NEXT PHASE • Full pain-free jaw opening ≥40 mm maintained • Eating all food textures without restriction • Independent self-management program in place • Stress and bruxism management strategies implemented
